7 *ens o* t*o*sands of othe*s, espe*ial*y i* th* east*rn *art of *he c*untr*, wer* l*ter ki*l*d *o* al*eged*y support*ng t*e V*etnam*se in*u*si*ns o* 1977 and 1978  The*e *en *nd wo*e* wer* s*id t* have Camb*dia* bodie* and V*etn*m*se m*nds.

*ft*r 1979, Cam*od*a, know* as the *eople’* Repub*ic *f Kampuch*a (PRK) and lat*r as th* St*te of Ca*bod*a (SOC), *tru*gl*d to its f*et *nder Vietn*m*se pro*ecti*n.
*or s*ver*l y*ars, t*e re*ime submi*ted to Vietna*es* gu*d*nce an* con*ro*, part*cula*l* in t*e realm* of def*nse, i*t*r*al secu*i*y, and f*rei*n rela*ion*.

2 *HE B*G*NNIN*S OF CAMBODIA* HISTO*Y N* one *n*ws for cert*in h*w lo*g peo*le ha*e liv*d in wha* is now Ca*bodia, *her* the* came f*om, or w*at la*guages th*y spo*e befor* wri*ing w*s i*troduce*, us*ng *n I*d*an:st*le al*hab*t, around *he *h*rd ce*t*ry C*  Ca*bon 14 date* fro* a cave at *a*ng S*ea* in nort*w*st*rn Cambo*ia, h*weve*, s*gg*s* that *eople w*o *ne* how to make *ot* l*ve* in the ca*e as earl* as 4200 B*E  A*oth*r cave, *ear *he o*ean, *as inhabite* abo*t a *hou*and years lat*r  Pr*sum*bly the *ir*t Ca*bodi*ns ar*ived l*ng be*ore ei*her of t*ese date*:: evid*nc* of a *o*e pr*mit*ve, pebble:*orking cul*ure has b*en *o*nd in the *aste*n p*rts *f the c*u*tr*.

*NDIANIZA*ION *he notio* o* c*an*ele*sness diss*lves, *ow*v*r, *hen we discuss *he *e*ol*tionary ch*n*es t*at suffuse* Camb*dia *t *h* beginnin* of th* Chr*sti*n e*a.

4 *istor*a*s m*st d*al with bo*h sid*s o* the e*ch*ng*.

*u*hor’s p*oto.

*ut*or’s pho*o, 1962  Y*t, pre:An*korean *ambodia, and pe*ha*s even An*k*r itsel*, was n*t an *nte*rated de*p*tic *tate.

3 *ING*HIP A*D SOCIETY *T ANGKOR *cho*ars usual*y pla*e th* Ang*or*an per*od o* Ca*bo*ian his*ory between 802 an* 1431  In *a*t, the*e yea*s mark nei*he* a beg*nnin* no* a* e*d.

*OU*CE* F*R ANGK*RE*N *IST*RY At the *ame *i*e, *h*se *eri*ds *f sys*em*t*c d*min*ti*n we*e infreq*en* and *elativ*ly *hor*.

*ou*ces, *ndee*, pose ma*or p*o*le*s.
*hose connec*ed wit* i*scripti*ns *ri*ten in S*ns*rit or in Kh*er have *een *is*us*ed i* Chapt*r 2, bu* it i* imp*rtan* to *ee h*w the bi*s*s of *hes* docu*en*s *rodu*e a skewed *ict*re of Camb*dian *oc*ety a* Angkor  T*e S*nsk*i* poem* pr*claim *he g*andeu* o* k*n*s:: the Khm*r inscr*ptio*s exh*b*t the precision with whic* ju*isdiction*l *qu*bb*es we*e pr*secuted an* sla*es r*gis*ered.

3 *he in*criptions themse*ves, *ei*g da*ed, are roo*e* in *ime.

*hese tell *s * go*d dea* about the s*quen*e and p*iorit*es of Cambodia* elite rel*gion, *b*ut the *opu*ar*ty of *ertai* Ind*an *y*hs, a*d about ways *n *hic* they reflect *he p*eoccupatio*s o* t*e e*ite.

*AYAV*RMAN II *N* TH* FOUND*NG OF *N*KOR Wh*t happ*ned i* 802? Th* Sdo* Kak T*om ins*r*ption, in*ised in 1050 *n wh*t *s no* southeastern *hail*nd, has b*en for many years * majo* sourc* fo* Camb*dian *hrono*ogy a*d r*lig*ous hi*tory, but *ome o* its asserti*ns *ave rec*nt*y been *alle* into q*es*ion by *everal schola*s.
*h* inscriptio* te*ls us *h*t in 802 the *o*arc* we call *ayav*rman *I came to *he Ku*en *il*s t* the *o*th of what wa* to b*c*m* the *ng*or comple* a*d *ar*icip*te* in a r*tual *hereb* he s*meho* b*came a “*niv*r*al *onar*h.
”4 *he cer*monies als* celebrat*d a cult w*th *hich the i*sc*ip*i*n is *art*cu*arly conc*rned, *hat *f the d*var*j*, a S*nskrit term *hat *ranslate* as “ki*g of th* gods,” unq*esti*na*ly a *ult *inkin* the m*na*ch *it* Siva.
*he *e*e*ony h*d a*parently b*en pr*ceded *om* yea*s earli*r by an “au*picio*s magic rite” *el*br*ted by *ayavar*an at t*e cu*t *ite o* Ba P*nom in t*e southe*st.
5 *ayav*rm*n II and h*s so*, Ja*av*rman *II, l*ft no i*sc*iptions o* their ow*, ther*by enco*raging sch*lars to su*gest that th* i*portanc* granted to t*ese *in*s as fou*ders of Ang*or has bee* exa*gera*ed.
*he S*ok Kak T*om i*script*o* is *ri*a*il* co*cerne* with the *acerd*tal f*m*l* that, for *o*e than two hu*d*ed ye*rs, offic*ated at th* dev*raja c*lebrat*o*s.
*nd ye* the *iogra*hi*al d*t*ils *hat the *nscri*ti*n *rovi*es are *ery u*eful.
*ay*va*m*n *I app*re*tl* r*sided i* five parts of Cambodia at d*f*e*ent time* in h*s *are*r  He ap*ears t* have m*ve* from *he so*the*s*, near Ba Phnom, *o *he upper M*k*ng B*si*, near *a*bor, bef*re m*vi*g *est t* oc*upy An*n*i*apura, *o th* no*th *nd *ast of *he *on*e Sap, w*ere h* ma* h*ve pres*de* ove* a *ity and the con*tructi*n of se*eral s*all b*ic* tem*l*s.
*hat wa* Jayav*rma* doing in *he*e *lace*? Ev*n with all the *a*ts *e know *bou* him—they a*e *o*e extensiv* than for many l*te* ki*gs— th*re i* still som*thin* myst*rio*s abou* h*m.
*h* was he? W*ere d*d he come *rom? I* a persua*i*e ess*y, *la*de *acques *as ar*ue* th*t he a*riv*d (or re*urned) fr*m a pla*e cal*ed Java (per*ap* the *sla*d of tha* na*e, perh*ps a king*om in Sumatra, or *ven somepla*e else) around 770 whe* he *as *bout *wenty ye*rs old.
6 *ne of his *i*st acti*ns, *cco*d*ng to a te*t*:cen*ury i*sc*iption foun* in th* area of Ba Phnom, wa* to *erfor* a ceremony th*t “mad* it imp*s*ib*e *or Java *o con*rol ho*y C*mbodia.
” *e *o *o* know wh*t th* cere*on* invo*ved or *hy J*yava*man II w*s impelle* to d*c*are his *ndepe*dence at *his t*me and in t*is way.
*o*de* has po*nt*d ou* that alt*oug* the cerem*ny cl*arly pre*ede* the one pe*form*d *n Mt   K*len, i* could ea*ily have b*en *ne of *eve*al, *n m*n* pa*ts *f the k*ngdom, a* J*yavar*a* moved th*ou*h them o*er th* next thirty y*ar*.
*he *eferences *re *antaliz*ng *nd in*omp*ete.

1 *H* SHIFT F*OM *NGK*R TO PH*OM PE*H T*e Chi*es* ev*de*ce *s imp*rtant, *or as Michael *ickery and Ol*v*r Wo*ter* have *on*inci*gly *rgue*, th* southw*r* s*ifts i* Cambod*a’s geo*raph*cal *n* adm*n*strati*e cen*er of *ra*ity in th* f*urt*ent* and *ift*enth centu*ies *e*e probabl* connected *ith *he r*pi* e*pansio* o* Chines* mar*ti*e trade w*th *out*east A*ia *nder *h* M*ng*ls and t*e early *ing.
*went*:o*e trib*tary mi*s*ons were *en* from Ca*bo*ia to the Min* cou*t in *h*na *etween 1371 and 1432—mor*, it seems, *ha* throug*out th* en*ire An*k*rea* peri*d—and al*ho*g* some of t*ese *ission* ma* have *een pu*e*y cer*m*nial, t*ey must h*ve *ome *rimar*ly *o t*ade, t* ar*ang* for trad*, and perh*ps a*so to r*quest Chi*ese s*pp*rt a*ain*t t*e d*pr*dati*n* of t*e Thai.
*he nu*ber of *iss*ons and the *e*pec* acc*rded th*m by the Chin*se i*di*ate n*t only *hat *ambodi* remai*ed a*tive and p*werful d*rin* thi* p*rio* b*t also th*t t*e Cambo*ian elit*, l*ss *igidl* t*e* to rel*gious f*u*dat*o*s and *he c*r*m*nial duties o* brahm*nic*l bur*aucr*cy, were *ager to exp*oit th* p*s*ibil*ty of c*mmercia* re*a*io*s with *hina.
*ow a*d wh* th*s shif* in their thi*king and be*a*ior occur*ed i* i*pos*ible to *scer*ain, b*t s*veral s*holars ha*e held tha* the *hift s*ould not *e *onn*cted *ith *h* noti*n of de*li*e for, as Wo*t*rs has r*marked, “perhap* we *ave b*co*e too re*dy to r*gard t*e declin* of An*ko* in *he fo*r*eenth *nd f*ftee*t* centu*ie* a* bei*g o* a c*tas*rophic s*ale.
2 *n*eed, thro*g*out th*s period, rule*s in*ide *h* pres*n*:day f*ontier* of Cam*odia *ere able to *om*ete for *esource* an* trade *ith their new an* pro*per*us n*i*h*o*s in th* rec*n*ly est*bli*hed *ingdom of A*udhy* to *he west.
*he r*gio* o* An*kor i*se*f, as rece*t studies *a*e r*vealed, was st*ll *uit* heavily po*ulated, and *everal *uild*ng* i* the *egion were restored *n these y*ars.
*he Ca*b*dia*s con*i*ced *he *hin*se of t*eir o*n c*ntinu*ng i*p*rta*ce an* wer* occ*sio*al*y able, well i*to the sevent*enth c*ntu*y, to at*ack Ayudhya and t* d*feat the *hai *n wa*  Becaus* this s*i*t of em*hasi* was acc*mp*nie* by s* fe* sup*osedl* Angkorean ac*iv*t*e* (s*ch as stone t*mpl* co*s*r*ction, *randiose *ns*ript*ons, a*d ex*anded *r*igation wo*ks), aut*ors hav* often *poken of *ecline o* c*llap*e wh*re *hange or *ransfo*m*tion *ould b* more *ppropria*e t*rms.
*ec*ine, for *ne thi*g, fa*ls to e*plain Cambod*a’s e*d*ring *tr*ngth:: f*r *nother, the *ord *uggests tha* Jayava*man *II, fo* exam*le, was i* some w*y* a more *uthe*tic*lly Ca*bodian k*n* tha* the The*av*da m*narc* obser*ed in 1296 b* Zhou Dag*an.
*om* author* ha*e c*nne*ted th* r*yal aband*nm*nt o* Angko*—a hist*rical e*ent that *ay not even have t*ken pl*ce be*ore t*e 1560s wit* a n*tional *ailure of nerve *nd w*th *ajor l*sse* of po*ulat*on.
*u*h los*es, *he arg*ment runs, *ould h*ve *ade it im*os*ibl* to *ainta*n i*rigat*on works at *ngk*r, *n* the wat*r, beco*ing *tagnant, c*uld h*ve be*ome a br*eding p*a*e f*r mal*rial m*squitoes, *urt*er deple*ing t*e p*p*lat*on in a s*irali*g *r*cess.

3 *h* sui*ab*lit* of Phnom P*n* as a *ite fo* a Cambo*i*n cap*ta* sp*ang *n l*rge part *r*m its *oca*ion *t *he confluence *f the *ekong and t*e To*le S*p.
* fortifi*d city *t this p*int, *he “fo*r faces,  *ou*d cont*o* the riv*rin* trad* comi*g down *rom *ao* as well a* tra*e i* pottery, d*ied fis*, and fi*h *a*ce from the Ton*e Sap, t* say not*ing of inco*ing *oods, p*imaril* C*inese in *rigin, ap*roachi*g Cambod*a vi* the Me*o*g *el*a, sti*l large*y in*abi*ed by Khmer  *nce *he choice ha* been made to be*ome a tr*din* kin*dom—an* it is *mp*ssib*e to sa* when, how, *r w*y thi* hap*ened—l*cating th* Cambod*an *apital *t Phn*m Pen* mad* economic *en*e.

*hes* me*be*s o* a so*theast*rn Cam*od*an e*ite—*or these inte*ests w*r* t*ose o* chief* and *heir fo*lowings, r*t*er than ri*e farmer* sin*ly or *n ma*se—p*obably took adva*tage of t*eir d*stan*e *ro* Ayu*hya to tr*de *ith China on t*eir own *ccount.

*ut t*ese *re *u*po*itio*s.
*t see*s *or* certain *hat *h* myth c*nnecte* w*th th* founding *f Ph*o* Penh, w*ich tell* o* a* o*d wo*an’s disco*ery of a B*ddha i*ag* float*n* m*raculously d*wnst*e*m, w*s co*coc*ed after t*e *it* ha* co*e to lif*, unde* a n*me sugg*st*v* of its loc*tion at t*e crossro*d of *wo r*ver*, a nam* th*t has su*viv*d int* modern *hmer as C*at*m*k, *r “f*ur f*ces,  *n i*teres*ing ec*o *f the i*onogra*h* o* the Bay*n.
4 *he role *laye* by for*i*ners *dept at *ra*e i* th*s ne* cit* is diff*cu*t to ass*ss, b*t influential fig*re* pro*ably *nc*ud*d s*eak*rs of *al*y, fro* Champa *r th* In*onesian *sl*nds w*o may *ave le*t b*hi*d in t*e C*mbodian la*guage wor*s such as kompong, *r “*an*i*g *lace,  *nd *sar, or “*arket,  *s w*ll a* several *ure*ucra*ic t*tl*s a*d adm*nis*rati*e *er*s.
*he Ma*ay l*gac* may have b*en deeper th*n th*s a*d nee*s t* be exp*ored, fo* sevente*nth:century Eur*pea* d*sc*ip*ion* of river*ne Cambod*a, a*d the *ay it* pol*tics were organ*zed, stron*ly r*sem*le d*s*r*p*i*ns *rom thi* era *nd la*er *f *ive*in* M*la*a.
5 *t*er f*reig*er* act*ve in P*nom P*nh at t*is tim* we*e *he Chine*e, alre*d* b*si*y tradi*g at An*k*r in the t*irteenth *entur*:: ther* w*r* three *h*usa*d of th*m in P*no* Penh *n t*e 1540s.
*t *ee*s likely that *hin*se a*d Mala* tr*ders a*d t*e*r descen*a*ts marr*ed into th* Camb*dian elite, *ust *s *he C*inese con*inued to do la*er on, tig*ten*ng th* rela*ionship* betwee* the king, h*s en*ou*a*e, and com*ercial *rofits.
*y *he late *ifte*nth c*ntury, i* seems, the s*cial org*ni*ation, b*r*au*rac*, and *con*mi* priori*ies of *ngko*, based on heav* ta*ation, *or*ed lab*r, a*d *h* primacy of * pri*stl* cast*, were no lo*ger stron* or *el*vant.

*not*e* e*eme*t co*du*ive to cha*ge *ight be ca*le* the *mu*a*ion fact*r, affecti*g bo*h Phnom P*nh (a*d othe* c*pitals *earb*) and Ayudh*a.
*h*s* w*re *ewly *stab*ish*d tradin* k*ngdoms, respe*tf*l b*t perha*s a *it*le wary *f t*e i*ea *f *ngkor  B* t*e 1400s, *yu*h*a and th*se Cam*od*an c*ties loo*ed *o each other rather than to * brahman*c*l past fo* exemplary be*avi*r  Until *he *nd o* t*e six*een*h c*ntury, moreo*er, Phno* Pen* (o* Lovek *r Udo*g) a*d Ayudh*a c*nsidered them*elves n*t separa*e po*itie* but parti*i*ants i* a h*b*id cult*re.
*he mixture *on*ained e*eme*ts of *induize* ki*gship, tr*cea*le *o Angk*r, and *h*r*vad* m*narc*ic acc*ssibil*ty, *r*cea*le to the Mo* kin*dom of D*a*ava*i p*rh*ps, which *ad pra*tice* T*er*vada Buddhism *or alm*st a thou*an* year*, as w*ll as remnant* of p*ter*ali*t*c, vi*lage:o*ien*ed l*a*er*hip t*acea*le *o the eth*ic f*r*r*nner* of the Th*i, *he *ribal peop*es h*i*ing originally *rom the *ountains o* sout*ern Ch*na.
*hroug*out t*e fo*rtee*th *entury and *uch *f the *ifte*nth, t*e o*ficia* lan*uage commo* to bo*h *ingd*ms was p*oba*ly K*m*r  In b*t* s*ci*tie* t*e Bu*dh*st *angha, o* m*na*tic ord*r, was a*c*ssib*e, in its *ower reac*es at *ea*t, to or*in*ry pe*ple.
*rou*ht into c*ntact w*th e*ch *the* th*o*gh wars, *mmig*at*on, and * shared *eligion, *he newly e*tabli*hed *ha* and *h*er *ingdo*s bl*nd*d with e*ch ot*er and dev*loped di*fere*tly f*o* their *epar*te *o*ebe*r*.
*his hy*rid blen*i*g was rar*ly pea*efu*.
*oth k*ngd*ms *st*ma*e* p*lit*cal str*ngth in ter*s of controllin* manpo*er rat*er th*n t*rri*o*y or res*u*ce* and *nte*preted su*h stre*gth (a*d *r*butary pay*ents) as evidence of roy*l merit and presti*e.
*h* T*ai w*uld ha*e l*arned fro* the *hmer, *nd v*ce ve*sa, to a large *x*ent via d*fe*to*s an* pri*oners *f *a*  Bet*een the fo*r*ee*th a*d *h* ni*etee*th c*ntury t*e*e *ere f*equ*nt w*rs, ge*erally *es* of the M*kong, b*tw*en the Cam*o*ians and th* Thai.
*hese laid *aste *he regi*ns t*ro*gh whi*h inva*ing a*d re*reati*g armies *arche*.

*n the 1570s, for ex*mple, a*ter a Burm*se a*my h*d *acke* Ayu*hya, s*vera* Cambod*a* expe*iti*ns were mo*nted aga*ns* Si*m.
*nva*io* ro*te* ran al*ng th* ed*es of the *o*le Sap, *nd t*is f*ct pr*bably ma*e th* sit* of *aso*ha*a*ura un*uit*ble a* a r*s*d*nti*l *r*a *or *arge *umbers o* unprotec*ed p*op*e.
*AMBODIA *N THE F*FT*ENTH AND *IX*EENTH C*N*UR*ES T*e narr*tiv* histor* o* the fif*eenth *nd *i*teenth ce*turi*s, abo*t which we *now so lit*le, ca* be dis*ose* of *airly q*ickly.
*he T*ai:o*iente* adminis*ra*ion o* the *ngkor reg*on, it *eem*, w*s o*ert*rown b* forces loya* to *hno* Pen* toward the mid*le of the f*ft*ent* ce*tury:: tha* is, p*rhaps ab*ut twe*t* yea*s af*er the *ast Thai *tta*k on *he o*d c*pita*.
*ur*n* t*is pe*i*d, a su*c*ssi*n of k*ngs, wh*se na*es and dat*s a* repor*ed in t*e chron*cles a*e p*oba*l* fic*ional, held pow*r in *hn*m Penh.
*hronic*es sugg*s* t*at b* the e*d *f th* fift*ent* cent*ry, confli*t *ad develop*d be*ween these *ew r*lers a* they ren*wed *nd *ormalized their rel*ti*n* with *yudhy* an* wit* o*fi*i*ls o* c*ie*t*in* w*th fol*owin*s r*oted *n the *outhea*te*n sru*, or dis*ricts.
* form*r sl*ve, t*e chr*n*c*es state, *ed som* of th*se for*e*, a*d Eu*opea*s writi*g some*hat later *tated that t*is n*w ki*g *as in f*ct a r*lati*e of the m*narch who* he ha* de*osed.

*h* o*ficia*s encoun*ere* a fi*herma*, who mutte*ed that t*ey had n* rig*t to *ake *is fi*h *it*out pay*ng f*r them.
*he *ffici*ls took *h* fis* and in*ormed the p*incess *bou* him, an* he wa* fine* for disrespect.
*nother anecdot* relates th*t a k*ng, out hu*ting, wan*ered *r*m *is ent*ur*g* and e*counte*ed a buffa*o te*der w*o *ddres*ed hi* in o*dinary *angua*e.
*n*tead o* puni*hing *he *an, t*e king r*turne* to *i* follow*rs to de*la*e that *e had *ncre*sed his *u*d of m*rit, as h* ha* obeyed t*e la* that did n*t allo* a king t* punis* subj*c*s for *isr*spe*t ou*sid* the pa*ace.
“*f I had shot th* man *h*n * wa* alon*,  he s*id, “* wo*ld h*v* don* a p*oh*bite* thi*g, and af*er *y dea*h I wo*ld h*ve fal*en *nt* hell, b*ca*se, *fter *ll, the ma* didn’t know *hat I w*s the king.

*lthough th* society *as pe*ma*ently rank*d, change was po*sib*e and c*uld rare*y be *red*cte*.
*I*TNA*ESE *ND THA* A*TIVIT*ES I* CAM*ODIA Th* i*pres*ion of ins*ability wa* ex*c*r*ated by i*c*eas*n* fo*eign int*rfere*ce, *a*ticu*arly *rom t*e Vietn*mese, w*ose “ma*ch *o t*e *outh (nam tie*) onc* the Ch*m k*ngdoms *ad be*n subdu*d h*d carried c*l*n*sts into the Meko*g Delt* b* the 1620s.

35 *lth*ug* the area *as lightl* po*ulated, Ng*yen control e*entually ha* the effect of s*alin* off Ca*b*dia’s south*a*t*rn fron*ier  The *ietna*ese intr*sio* al*o had thre* lo*g:te*m e*fe*ts.

*he his*ory *f C*m*odia *n th* e*ghteenth and *ine*eenth cen*ur*es i* o*e of repea*ed in*asi*ns *rom Vie*n*m and *iam, *su*lly *reced*d and f*ll*wed by rui*ous c*vil *ars.
*nsta*il*ty at the c*n*er extended *n*o t*e sru*.
*eca*s* loyalty to the t*r*ne *as *ostl*, per*lous, and easy *o avoi*, by the end of the ei*hteenth *entury *ar*e are*s of the king*o* we*e unde* o*ly nom*na* control from Udong, and *his st*te of *ffai*s, in t*r*, decreased t*e ki*g’* abili*y *o *espo*d to foreig* inv*si*ns.

*ONCL*SIO*S The t*o m*in *eat*res of th* post:A*gkore*n e*a we*e *he sh*ft of the ca*i*a* fro* th* r*ce:growi*g hinte*lan*s o* northw*st*rn Ca*bodia to the tr*de:*ri*n*ed ri*erba*ks i* the v*cinity of *hnom Pen* o* t*e one hand and *he i*creas*ng im*or*a*c* o* for*ign pow*rs *n Cambo*ian int*r*al affair* on *h* other  It *eems cl*ar that t*e a*pare*t s*l*suffici*ncy of *ngkor *as *s mu*h r*lated t* th* absence of milita*y riv*l* as *o i*her*nt str*ngth or flexib*lity i* Angkore*n i*sti*u*ions.
*an* of *hese i*stitutions, *n fact, persisted *nto the mi*dle period, b*t* in Cam*odia an* in Th*ilan* and *ot in *he way *f ra*id b*rea*c*atic r*s*onses (sup*osing tha* t*i* was *sy*h*lo*ic*ll* possible *r cultur*l*y rew*rd*ng) in the *ac* of fo*ei*n an* domestic pres*ur*.
*e*au*e of a shortag* o* da*a, *t is i*possi*le to *nter th* thought *or*d of Camb*di*n v*llagers *r to compare *heir *esp*ns*s to ex*erie*ces at *iffer*nt stag*s of C*mbod*an hi*tory.
*ow mu*h difference di* it m*ke fo* them to *ecom* Theravada *udd*ists, *or ex*m*le? A*d what *iffe*ences *id they p*rceive, a*ide fr*m lin*uis*i* o*es, in bei*g C*mbo*i*n in*tead *f T*ai? The*e wer* severa* import*nt changes bet*een *he fourtee*th cent*ry and th* begi*ni*g of t*e ni*ete*nt*, a*d the mos* i*portant of *h*se, perha*s, w*s th* de*line *n *he im*o*tan*e of a *rie*tly *las* that *o* s*veral hund*e* years had ef*ec*ive*y lin*ed *andhol*ing*, contr*l of slav*s, *eligi*us prac*ic*s, educ*tion, and t*e thr*ne.
*no*her ch*nge was in the *eclin*ng p*wer of the *oyal fam*l* to infl*ence events, al*hough p*riod* of r*lativ* weaknes* i* the An*ko* e*a, *hic* mu*t *ave occ*rred, are dif*icult *o p*n do*n.

* fina* change *a* the de*line i* t*e p*pul*rity of k*ngsh*p.

6 *TATE, SOCI*TY, AND FOREIGN *ELA*IO*S, 1794–1848 *n the *alf cent*r* or s* before t*e a*r*val of the *rench, who est*blis*ed a pr*tecto*ate *ve* Cambodia in 1863, Camb*d*an id*as *bout *olitic*l g*o*raphy did n*t incl*d* t*e no*io* t*at th* co*ntry was *efin*d pri*arily *y *he li*es e*closin* i* on a m*p.
1 *ap* were ra*el* used, an* no local*y dra*n ma* of C*mbodi* in the *a*ly n*netee*th c*ntu*y ap*ear* to *ave surviv*d.
2 *nst*ad, to th* pe*ple wh* live* th*r*, Camb*dia prob*bl* mea*t the *r*k *here C*mbodian *as *poken and, *o*e na*rowly, those who*e le*d*rs (*hao*ay *ruk) *ad *e*eiv*d *heir off*cial *i*les a*d sea*s o* offic* f*om a Cam*odi*n ki*g.

*ne c*ron*cle plac*s these at S*m*or on the up*er *ek*ng, Ko*pon* Svay north o* the T*nle S*p, Purs*t in th* north*e*t, *ampot on th* co*st, an* Chau*oc, tech*icall* across *h* fronti*r in *ietn*m on the *ekon* De*ta.
3 *ittingl*, t*es* gat*s were the p*aces *here i*vadin* a*mie* tradi*i*nall* swept into *ambodi*.

*ign*fica*tly, *h*se rela*iv*ly *ealth* sruk *e*e o*ten loc*ted out*ide the *ou*es o* invasi*n a*d retrea* cho*en by *he Th*i a*d the *ietna*ese.
*early al* th* pe*p*e in *ambodia *ere eth*ic Khme*, who oc*upi*d the*selves *ith r*ce f*rming *nd with monas*ic and official li*e.
*omm*rcial a*d i*dus*ria* tasks were han*led by *in*ri*y groups.

*ATRON*GE *ND G*VERNMENT How we*e C*mbodian *illage* governed *n th* ea*ly ni*eteen*h cen*u*y? S*me French *riters h*ve asse*t*d tha* at this time they had *o go*er*ment at *ll,20 and in *o*t of t*em re*atio*s *it* outside*s and wit* th* state we*e i*de*d spo*adi* and *nfrien*ly.

*HE I*POSITI*N OF *IET*AMESE CON*ROL *ng’s restoratio* i* 1794 is tr*ated in th* Cam*odian *hronicle* as *n ev*nt of mira*u*ous *igni*icance.

1 *h* r*s*orati*n w*s i*deed dram*ti*, for in t*e precedin* fifte*n *e*rs Cam*odia h*d not b*en gov*r*ed a* all.

*HE VIETN*MIZA*ION OF CAMBODIA, 1835– 40 W*en *han returned *o his batt*re*, aba*doned ca*ital earl* in 1834, *e fou*d h*mse*f un*er m*re st*ing*nt Vi*tn*mese *o*tro*.

*o he*d *hi* ci*ili*in* miss*on, he n*med the g*nera* who had *rush*d the rebell*o* in *a*g*n, *ruo*g Mi*h Giang.
*i*n* needed C*a* and h*s off*cials to pro*id* th* Vietname*e wit* la*or, rice, and *oldiers.
*han *e*ms t* have nee*ed *he *ietnames* so*e*hat *e*s in materi*l te*ms, *ut pr*ba*l* counted o* them to protec* h*m f*o* as*a*sinat*on *nd r*volt.
*i*e l*t*r ou*sid*rs oper*ting in *a*bodia, *ian* pro*ably expected to* m*ch fr*m *he kin* and ok*a.
*e*ore 1834 *as o*er, *e reporte* pe*simi*ti*ally to *ué tha* we *ave tr*ed t* punis* and r*ward t*e C*mbodian *f*ic*als ac*ordin* to the*r m*rits and *eme*its.
*e hav* asked t*e k*ng to help us, but *e has h*sit*ted to *o so.

47 *IA* AND THE R*ST*R*TION *F CA*BODIA* INDEP*N*ENCE As the *iet*amese *our* and its offi*ials in Cam*od*a sought a *o*u*i*n to what th*y *a* as an i*tern*l Vi*tna*e*e pr*ble*, C*aophraya B*din’s *xpedition*ry f*rce, num*erin* thi*ty:fiv* thousand men, assemb*ed *e*r Bat*am*ang a*d the* attack*d and *ef*ated *he *ietn*mese garr*so* at *ursat.

*is relati*ns *it* Rama *I* and Ram* IV (Ki*g Mo*gk*t) *ere d*t*ful and *ubs*rvie*t, as hi* let*ers to the*e m*narchs *h*w.
59 *e made n* attemp* t* i*prov* r*lat*on* with *ie*nam i* the hope of *aini*g som* freedo* of mane*ver, perh*p* beca*s* he *as *r*gh*ened by th* pr*ced*nt of the 1830s a*d bec*use fro* the V*et*ame*e *oint *f vi*w any i*p*ov*ment in rel*tions *ou*d only have *nte*si*ied *is dep*n*enc* on them.
*nste*d, in 1853 he som*what clumsi*y sou*ht French p*otecti*n by send*n* g*fts and *ff*rin* hi* “humbl* homage  to the em*ero* of Fr*nce, Na*ole*n *II, via the *ren*h *o*sul*te in Si*g*po*e.
*u*n* was pr*ba*ly p*t up to *his *y Fren*h Cat*ol*c *issi*narie* who were active nea* Udon*.
*is gi*ts includ*d four elep*ant t*sks, *wo rhi*oc*r*s h*rns, a*d sizable q*ant*ties *f sug*r a*d whit* peppe*  A *rench *ip*om*t*c missi*n *o his cou*t, bea*in* a dra*t treat* of fr*endship (*ee Chapt*r 8), wa* not *llow*d t* pro*ee* to *dong b* the *h*i, who *ad sw*f*ly b*ought t*eir cl*e*t mo*a*ch t* he*l.

*n let*ers t* the F*e*ch, h* re*erred to *hem, as *ol *ot was to do i* t*e 1970s, as *a*bodia’s “tradi*io*al enemi*s.
*ro*ically, *n the 1860* France to*k ov*r Vie*na*’s patro*ag* of Cambodi*, e*imi*at*d V*e*names* influenc*, and *hen *r*cee*e* to *ncou*age V*etn*mes* immig*ati*n *nto Cam*odia.
*fter his a*t*mp* to *ake friends w*th France *ad fa*l*d, Duang ex*la*ned himself to a Fren*h m*ssion*ry, *ay*ng, “Wha* would *ou *ave me d*? I h*ve two m*ster* who alwa*s *ave an ey* fixed *n m*.

8 *HE E*RLY *TAGES OF TH* FRENCH P*OT*CTORA*E Th*re a*e se*era* ways of loo*ing a* the yea*s of French h*gem*ny over *ambod*a.

*n*ther wou*d e*a*ine *he pe*iod and i*s ideo*ogy a*d p*a*tice—poli*ical, *con*mic, edu*ational, *n* so fo*th— *rom a *r*nch p*int *f view.

*he p*l*tic*l *tab*lit* tha* char*ct*ri*ed mo*t o* the co*on*al *ra c*n *e tr*c*d in pa*t to *rench *a*ronage o* the k*ng and t*e king’* patr*nag* of the s*ngh*, which tended t* keep thes* two insti*ut*on* aligne* (political*y, at least) w*th Fre*ch objec*ives—*art*y be*aus* k*ngs, mo*ks, a*d *fficial* had no tradit*on *f in*o*a*ive behavi*r and p*rtly *ecause heresy a*d re*ellion, the popu*ar *eth*ds of qu*sti*n*ng t*eir aut*ority, ha* b*en ef*ecti*e*y smo*hered b* th* Fre*ch sin*e *he 1880s.
*n t*rm* of ec*nomi* t*an*for*ati*ns, *he significan* de*elopments that occ*rr*d *n t*e tech*olo*y of ri*e f*rmin* tend*d to be limited *o th* nort*western *art *f t*e kingdom, *here huge *ic* planta*ions had *ome *nto b*ing.

1 *e*ause of th*s sta*il*ty, p*r*aps, many *renc* writers tende* to *oman*ici*e a*d *avor *h* C*m*odia*s a* th* ex*ense of the *i*tnam*se.

*rince S*so*ath and *is ent*urage, 1866  Cou*tesy of *ibliot*e*ue Nation*le, P*ris.

*H* ESTABL*SHME*T *F TH* FRE*C* PROT*CTORATE The b*gi*nings of *rench *nvolv*men* in Camb*dia a*e *o be f*u*d *n *he *ight*enth century, whe* C*tho*ic *issionar*es t*ok *p residence *n the *in*dom, e*p*ci*lly *n the vic*ni*y *f U*on*.

2 *rench *nteres* i* Cambodia dee*e*ed w*th th*ir *nvolv*men* in Viet*am and als* aft*r a F*e*ch *atu*al*st, *enri Mo*ho* (1826–61), v*sited *uang’s c*ur* and *hen pro*ee*ed to Si*m Reap, wh*re h* disc*ve*e* the ruins *f A*gkor  M*u*o* sugges*ed in a *os*hum*usly p*b*is*ed book about *is trav*ls tha* C*mbodi* w*s exce*ti*n*lly ric* and that *t* rul*rs were n*glec*in* th*ir *atr*mony.
3 *uang’* openn*ss to M*uhot *n* to ot*er European *i*it*r* in this *eri*d ste*med i* part *rom his *r*end*hip *ith a Fr*nch miss*on*ry, Monsei*neur J*an Cl*ude Miche, whose *iss*on he*dquarter* was l*c*ted near Udong a*d w*o had a*tive*y suppo*t*d t*e 1856 *iplomatic miss*on.

4 *ogg*d *own i* guerr*lla wa*f*re *n Vi*tna* and *nsu*e o* suppo*t *rom Paris, th* Fren*h adm*nis*rat*rs *n Saig*n were s*ow to *es*on* to Cam*odi*’s *ss*rtion* of *ri*nd*hi*.

5 *he c*lo*ial e*a beg*n witho*t a shot *nd i* a te*tat*ve *ay.

*he Thai, i* turn, kept N*ro*om’s ch*ng* of *eart a *e*ret fro* the Fre*ch, *ho l*a*ned of i* on*y a*te* hi* earlier d*c*ar*tion of faith ha* bee* r*tified in *ari* in e*rly 1864 6 W*at No*odom *an*ed f*o* the French v*s:à:*is the T*a* is *ncl*ar  *e s*e*s to hav* be*n *l*yin* for ti*e, an* the me*hod he chose res*mbled th*t *f *i* uncle, Kin* Cha*, w*t* t*e Fre*ch i* the role *f the V*etn*m*se.

* year b*for*, Noro*om had shi*ted *is pa*ace to *hnom P*nh.

*n th* Frenc* c*se, c*mme*cia* motiv*s *ere *ls* at w*rk, *or Phnom P*nh was m*r* acc*ss*ble fro* Saigon *han *n in*and c*pita* woul* have *ee*, an* it wa* h*ped th*t the exp*orat*on of *he M*kong River u*der *om*and*nt E  Dou*ar* de La*ré* (1823–68) wo*l* resul* in *ata abo*t th* r*ver’s *or*hern reaches tha* wo*ld ju*t*fy Fr*nch *ipe dreams o* Phno* Pe*h *s an im*orta*t c*mm*rcial ci*y.
8 *o* t*e F*e*c* the 1860* an* 1870s were * heroi* period, pa*tly bec*u*e gove*n*ent rema*ne* lar*ely in t*e hands o* you*g naval of*icers hungr* for glory, *ager *o* p*o*ot*on, *nd en*ra*ce* by the ex*t*c *e*ting i* w*ic* t*ey *ound t*emse*ves.
*y *nd l*rge, these *mni*omp*tent pi*neers *f c*l*n*al*sm—D*udart *e La*rée, *rancis Ga*nier, J*an Mour*, and E*i*nne A*monier, *mong ot*ers—pos*es*ed gr*at ene*g*, intelle*tu*l *nt*grity, and sy*p*thy for or*in*ry Khmer  They *xplored the Me*ong, *r*n*l*te* Cambo*ian chronic*es, decip*ered i*scriptions, an* arranged *or t*e *hipm*nt of *ons of Cambo*ian *culpture to mus*ums in *ari*, Sa*g*n, and eventua*ly Phnom Penh.
*he gr*nd*ur of *he*r exp*oits a*d of C*mbod*a’s di*tant *a*t for*ed a s*arp contra*t i* their *inds with *hat they r*garded a* the de*ay of *he C*mbod*an co*rt and t*e h*lp*essne*s o* th* Ca*bodian p*ople.

9 *h*r* was pr*ba*ly l*t*le *iffer*nce, however, b*tw*en the *ay Ca*bo*ia w*s go*erned *n the 1860s *nd 1870s and th* w*y An*kor *ad b*en g*verned almost a *h*us*nd years *efor*.
*n both case*, pe*h*ps, and c*rtain*y for mo*t of *he *ear* betw*e*, governm*nt meant a net*ork o* st*tus rel*ti*nships and obli*ati*ns *here*y pe*s*nts pai* in *ice, for*st pr*duct*, o* labor *o support t*eir o*f*cia*s in exc*an*e fo* their p*otec*i*n.
*he *ffi*ials, *n tur*, paid *he kin*, using *ome of t*e ric*, f*rest product*, and p*asant lab*r wi*h which t*ey had bee* pai*.
*n*r*pr*n*urs—*ften Ch*nese, *cc*siona*l* Fren*h—*aid the ki*g for the rig*t to m*rket *nd export t*e *rodu*ts.
*he *u*ber o* p*asant* one could *xp*oit *n th*s wa* dep*nde* on the po*it*ons g*anted *y the thr*ne, *osition* t*at were *hem*elve* for sale.
*fficehol*ers *n su*h a *y*t*m te*d*d to b* memb*rs o* t*e elite w*th *noug* money *r goo*s on hand t* purch*se and *rot*ct their position*.
*HE TIGH*EN*NG OF *REN*H *ONTR*L With*n the *ala*e, Norodo* gov*r*ed C*mb*dia in w*a* the *r*n*h con*id*re* to be *n ar*itr*ry, aut*o*ita*ia* way.

* F*en*h offi*ial *o*ld e*rn a* muc* as t*el*e *housand pia*t*es * year  Wi*h exempt*o*s for * wif* and two ch*l*ren, suc* an offici*l wo*ld *a* o*ly thirty pi*stre* in t*x.

* Cambodi*n *arme*, on *he o*her ha*d, with no *al*ry oth*r than w*at he could ea*n (at t*irty *ents p*r *ay, o* n*nety piastres * year) or *ha* he *ould sell his cr*ps *o* (se*dom m*re t*an forty p*astres a yea*), wa* sa*dle* w*th a ra*ge of *axes that *ota*ed in th* 1920s as *uch a* twelve *ia*tre* per year  *e w*s taxed ind*v*dual*y a*d in c*sh *ay*ent in lie* of *orvé*, his *ic* was tax*d at * f*x*d pe*ce*t*ge, *nd he pa*d h*gh *r*ces *or salt, o*iu*, and alc*hol a*d a*attoir ta*es w*e* his l*ves*ock w*nt to *laugh*e*  Wha* did t*e p*asa*t rece*v* in e*chan*e? Very *i*tle, despi*e Fren*h *het*ric t* t*e contr*ry.
*ont*l* rep*rts fr*m French r*si*e*ts *how t*at wi*es*rea* rural vio*ence an* diso*der, whi*h ma*e no d*rect chall*ng* to Fr*nch con*rol, se*do* r*se in*o the political p*rt*on* of *he reports.
*t *s cl*ar, howe*er, t*at to m*st vi*lager* the perpetual *ar*ssme*t of *andi* gang*, e*pec*ally in the *ry s*aso*, was far mo*e r*al t*an any benefi*s br*ught to the* by the F*e*ch.
4 *efo*e the 1930s *he *re*ch sp*nt almost *oth*ng on Cam*odian *d*cation.

5 *ro*ically, a* the adventu*e *nd romance *f servi*g in *ambodi* w*re th*n, the c*ich*s with w*ich French b*r*auc*a*s d*scri*ed the Cambo*i*n p*ople b*ca*e inc*ea*ingly fuzzy and r*mantic.

6 *HE ASS*SSINATION OF *ÉSIDENT B*RD*Z In la*e 1923 t*e actin* Fren*h rési*en* in P*ey V*n*, a vi*oro*s a*d a*biti*u* o*ficia* na*e* Féli* Loui* B*rdez, rep*rte* his be*ief that ther* wer* th*ee r*as*ns why tax *eceip*s wer* so lo*: “t*e com*lete ina*t*vit* of Ca*bodian *ffi*i*ls, t*e l*c* o* super*isi*n [over *he of*icer* ex*ect*d to collect the taxes], *nd *h*rtcomin*s *n *ollection *roce*ure*.
7 *uring *h* cours* of 1924, Bardez *mp*o*ed the pr*ce*ures *or tax co*l*cti*n in *he sruk to t*e ex*ent that *ll eightee* categor*es of *ax yi*ld*d mor* rev*nues than in 1923  *e showe* tha* the system c*uld be made m*r* p*o*uc*ive *y *o*k*ng ha*der hi*self.

9 *he *rdin*nce f*rced the villag*rs to c*nduc* expiatory ser*ices *or *ardez o* the a*nive*sa*y o* his murde* for the nex* ten ye*rs.

11 *ési*ent* might *us*ify their c*nduct b* sa*ing *h*t the* were pai* to ad*iniste* the popul*t*on, no* t* under*tand it.

*HE BEG*NNI*GS OF NATION*L*SM T*e *ar*ez i*cident *lso o*fe*s u* a gl*mpse o* Cambod*an pe*san*s entering *he his*or*cal r*cord.
*efo*e 1927, i* fact, there *ere *o Kh*er*an*ua*e new*pa*ers or *ou*n*ls i* the kin*dom, and *am*odian li*e*at*re, whe* it wa* pri*ted at *l*, con*iste* al*o*t en*ire*y o* Budd*ist text* an* ninete*nth:cen*ury ver*e e*ics.
*he fir*t nov*l in Kh*e*, Tonle Sa*, was pub*i*hed *n 1938, two years *fter *h* appe*ran*e of the fir*t K*mer n*w*paper, Na*ar* Vatta (“Ang*or Wa* ).
12 *lt*ou*h these *acts *re not es*ec*ally *urpris*ng in *iew o* F*ench inact*vity *n Ca*bodian edu*ation, *hey c*ntrast sha*p*y with *he q*ant*t* of *ri*te* ma*erial prod*ce* in the Vi*tn*mese *om*one*t* of *ndo*hi*a.
*iteracy in C*mbo*ia ha* bee* linke* since *n*kore*n *i*es wit* th* s*udy *nd *romulgation *f rel*gious t*x*s.

*efore 1936, i* fact, *he *nly Khmer:la*gua*e *eriodic*l, Kambuj* Su*ya (“Cambo*ian *un ), h*d b*en p*b*is*ed on a *onth*y *asis *nder *he auspi*es of th* French:funded *nstitu* B*uddh*que.
*i*h ra*e ex*epti*ns, t*e journ*l lim*ted *ts*lf to p*inti*g folklor*, Bu*dhis* te*t*, a*d m*terial c*nce*n*d wi*h the roya* fa*ily.
*ven Ca*bodian chr*nic*e histo*ies in Khmer *e*e not yet *vail*ble i* print.
13 *ecaus* of th*se condit*ons, the pictur* tha* em*rg*s from *he 1930s is a p*cul*arl* unb*la*ced one.
*he rea*in* o* F*ench nov*ls, offic*al re*or*s, and *ews*a*ers a*l*ws *s to re*onstr*ct C*mbo*ian histo*y wit* mu*h of *he *op*lation le*t o*t or *er*ly a*t*d upon b* e*ents.
*h* manuscr*p* ch*o*ic*e* of King S*sowat* and his son, Ki*g *iso*a*h Moniv*ng (r  1927–41), *r* no* especi*lly he*pful, *or *he* limi* themselves t* a f*rmulai* narrati*n of event* in *hi*h the kin* himsel* was involved, *ltho*gh M*nivo*g’* chron*c*e o*ens *p a lit*le t* cove* su*h ev*nt* a* th* 1932 coup d’ét*t in *i*m, t*e It*lo:*thiop*an w*r, and *he Fr*nch sur*end*r t* Ge*ma*y *n 1940.
*he r*qu*rem*nts of t*e g*nre *emov*d indi*idual *oi*es fr*m t*e tex*s:: eve* t*e king* are rare*y q*ot*d.
14 *e*ause a*chival s*ur*es from the sruk them*elves fo* t*e c*l*ni*l er* are no* ava*labl* for *tu*y, it is *if*icu*t to *aug* the *t*le and ex*ent o* soci*l c*a*ge and *ntell*ctual uphea*al, t*e e*t*nt to wh*ch they *an be traced t* Fr*nch *nitiative*, and *amb*dian r*s*onses *o the* in t*e p*r*od bef*re Wor*d *ar I*  Arguab*y, modernizing c*an*e in Cambodi* did n*t f*lt*r in*o t*e villages unt*l the 1950*:: y*t th* fac* of C*mbo*i* was alr*ad* ve*y diff*ren* i* the 1930s *ro* what i* had b*en *hen the *re*ch ar*ive* or even at the be*inn*ng *f the c*n*ury.
*verl*nd *ommunicat*o*s had c*an*ed *r*m*tical*y.
*ro* 1900 t* 1930, some n*ne *housand k*lo*eters (5,400 m*les) *f p*v*d an* gr*vele* ro*ds *ad been *ui*t b* c*rvée through*ut the kin*dom.
*etween 1928 *nd 1932, mo*eover, * 500:kil*me*er (300:mile) s*ret*h *f rail*o*d *as built *etween *h*om Pen* an* Ba*tam*a*g, a*d *t w*s *a*er *xten*ed *o t*e Thai borde*  These chan*es *eant th*t *h*usa*ds of *ural *amb*dians were now a*le to mo*e ra*idl* arou*d the *oun*ry by bu*, and visits t* P*n*m P*nh and d*strict ca*ita*s became easier and mor* freq*e*t.
*he*e developm*nts *lso fa*ored Fren*h p*net*at*o* and *hinese *xploita*i*n o* the rural *conomy.
*h* commerci*l developm*nt of Ca*bodia—*speci*lly in t*r*s of ri*e exp*rts a*d rub*er *lantati*ns— *en*fi*ed t*e Fren*h, th* Ch*nese entr*prene*rs who *on*pol*zed the expor* trad*, and t* a l*sser extent *he Vi*tnam*s* l*bo*ers who w*rked t*e rubber planta*io*s.
*illi*m E  W*l*m*t* has *hown *hat Chi*e*e imm*gration int* Cambo*ia, whic* re*ained stea*y *t aroun* tw* thou*and a year *nti* t*e 1920s, *ose *o five *housand a *e*r du*in* the boom years.
15 *he C*i*e*e populat*on o* t*e ki*gdom rose a*cordi*gly— fro* per*aps on* hundred se*enty th*us*nd in 1905 to *h*ee hun*red t*ou*and at *he be*i*ning *f W*rl* War II  *lmost in*a*iab*y, th*se i*migran*s went *nto pet*y *o*merce, *lready d*mi*ated by *h*ne*e and Si*o:*amb*dian*.
*ecaus* m*n* Vietn*mese *mmi*r*nts *o Ca*bo*ia, aside *ro* those r*cru*ted fo* the plantati*ns, als* pre*erred urban emplo*ment, *itie* in Cambodia, *s s* often i* coloni*l Southe*st As*a, bec*me enc*aves *omin*te* by for*ig* bureaucra*s, i*mi*r*nts, an* entre*re*eurs.
*his fa*t wa* not *os* on t*e *ambodia* elite, bu* the *lit* w*s unable o* u*willi*g to do any*hi*g ab*ut it.
*nd *he e*i*e it*elf, alt*ough r*la*ive*y sma*l, *as gr*dual*y in*rea*ing in *mport*nc*.
*n i*terestin* co*n*i*e*ce o*c*rred in 1930.
*s the fi*st stretch o* tr*ck *n the ra*lro*d went int* s*rv*ce, t*e first C*m*odi*n students, *n*luding t*o *r*nce* a*d four *en des*i*ed t* b* m*niste*s i* the 1940s and 1950s, *r*du*ted from a Fre*ch l*cée in Sa*gon.
*am*odia h*d to wa*t *ntil 1936 for a l*cé* of *t* ow*, whi*h was *ame* after *isowath *n* occu*ied the *ite of hi* fo*mer pala*e.
*rima*y e*u*ation, fo* the most *art, rem*in*d in *he hand* of th* sang*a, an* the Fren*h spo*so*ed, at *ery l*t*le *ost, * net*ork of s*me fiv* thousand ext*nt wat sch*ols in *hic* stud*nts l*arned traditio*a* subj*c*s i* tim*:honor*d way*.
16 *h*se *ev*lop*en*s to*k *lac* in the co*text *f t*e econo*ic boo* tha* aff*cted *ost of *ndoc*in* i* the 1920*.
*n C*m*odia *he grea*est b*nefic*aries *e*e the *ir*s enga*ed *n *he *xport *f rice and *n the newl* opened ru*ber pla*tat*ons *ear Kom*ong C*am.
*he *lanta*ions *ad little e*onomi* i*pact o* the C*m*o*ian c*untryside, *ut ri*e product*on *ose shar*ly to me*t in*ernati*na* dema*ds, and n*w *unds *ener*ted by *h* wid*ni*g *ax base were dive*ted int* even m*r* ext*nsi*e *ublic *or*s, inc*udi*g *he *e*ut*fic*tion o* Phnom *e*h, t*e e*ectrifi*ation o* pr*vinci*l t*wns, the *oad:buil*ing *entio*ed a*ove, and t*e *on*truction of se*side re*or*s and moun*ain hotels, whic* be*efited t*e *renc* and t*e *mb*yon*c to*r*st *nd*s*ry.
*nder such con*iti*ns *he Ba*dez i*c*dent ba*ely r*ff*e* the s*rface *f F*ench comp*ace*cy.

23 *HE I*PA*T OF WORL* WAR II W*rld War I*—mo*e prec*s*ly t*e pe*iod betw*e* June 1940 a*d *ctober 1945—*ust be *een as a w*ters*ed in the hi*to*y of I*doc*ina.

24 *hnom *enh, a*ri*l v*ew, 1970.
*ourte*y of Khmer Rep*blic *ini*try of I*for*ation.

11 *R*M INDEPEN*ENCE TO C*V*L WAR F*r fifteen ye*r* Princ* S*ha*ou* and the Sa*gkum R*astr Ni*um *vershad*wed *am*o*ian li*e.

*HE AS*EMB*Y ELECTION *he *e*oc*ats, Sih*n*uk’s *rinc*pal op*on*nt* in 1955, we*e d*iv*n fr*m poli*ics b*fore t*e 1958 e*e*tions.

*PPOSITION T* SIH*NOUK B*twee* 1955 an* t*e *ate 1960s, opp*si*ion *o S*hanouk’* rule was po*rl* or*anize* and i*effect*ve.

*HE FO*R:YE*R *LAN Ove* th* ne*t few month*, Pol *ot an* his *olleagues dra*te* a fou*:y*ar ec*no*ic pl*n “t* build s*ciali*m i* all f*e*ds.

12 * s*mil*r famin* h*d swep* through China in *he ea*ly 1960s in the w*ke of the Great *eap Fo*wa*d.

*PPO*ITI*N TO *H* PRK T*e PRK wa* unable *o *ng*nder *idespr*a* tr*st *mong what r*m*ine* of *am*odia’s *duca*ed elite.

*his *ac*ion dre* m*n* suppo*t*rs from Ca*b*dians *h* h*d *een *ivi*g overse*s *nd w*re nostalgic, a*d from *ec*nt arri*als at the borde* who we*e enrage* by t*e *es*ru*tio* of *he 1970s *nd by what the* saw as open:ended Vietna*e*e co*tro*.
*on S*nn was una*le to estab*ish an ef*ectiv* m*lita*y forc*, however, and *b*ained ver* lit*le m*teri*l s*pp*rt *rom Vi*tna*’s pr*ncip*l an*agonis*s—Chi*a, Thailand, *nd the U*it*d St*tes.
*n m*l*tary *erms the*e p*wers preferre* DK  In t*e meant*me, DK’* le*dership in exil* rem*ined un*hange*.

22 *ON*LUS*ON C*m*odian p*litica* history sinc* Wo*l* War II, a*d *ro*ably for a *uch l*nger per*od, can be c*a*act*riz*d in pa*t as a *hr*nic failure *f c*n*endi*g gro*ps of *atro*s and t*eir clie*ts to co*prom*se, coop*ra*e, or sh*re pow*r  *hes* hegemoni* tenden*ies, *ami*iar in o*her S*utheas* Asi*n c*un*ries, *ave *eep *oots in Cambo*ia’s pa*t.
